(4) Philippines' Boktokshin: 6.89 meters

The Far Eastern record was 7.07 meters, held by Oda Mikio. This time, the top three all broke the record. Nambu's score was very close to the world record of 7.89 meters. The progress of the Japanese is astonishing, and China can only lag far behind.

(IV) The High Jump Decisive Victory 123

Only one Chinese participant, Li Zhongsan, joined. The Japanese participants were Kimura Kazuo, Ono Misao, Murakami Masatake, and Utsuki Akira (four in total). The Filipino participants were Tolidoble, Reyes, and Alifo (three in total). All eight had considerable skill, and the competition was extremely fierce. When jumping to 1.80 meters, China's Li Zhongsan actually jumped over it in one attempt. At that time, all eight participants successively jumped over it. When the height was increased to 1.84 meters, the Filipino Reyes, the Japanese Murakami and Utsuki, and China's Li Zhongsan all failed after three attempts. Only the Japanese Kimura and Ono and the Filipino Alifo and Tolidoble remained. The height was then increased to 1.91 meters. The Filipino Tolidoble jumped over it in one attempt. The Japanese Kimura and Ono both needed two attempts to succeed. The height was then increased to 1.94 meters. Ono failed to clear it, but Kimura cleared it on the third attempt. It was then increased to 1.96 meters. The Filipino jumped over it in one attempt, and Kimura also cleared it on the third attempt. Afterward, it was increased to 1.98 meters. Kimura was exhausted and unable to jump. The championship was finally won by the Filipino Tolidoble. The Filipino then jumped again, achieving a score of exactly 2 meters. Kimura was second with 1.96 meters. Ono was third with 1.91 meters, and the Filipino Alifo was fourth with 1.84 meters. The Far Eastern record was 1.93 meters. This time, the top two both broke the record, and the first place's 2 meters was very close to the world record of 2.03 meters. The Chinese track and field coach, the American Mr. Smith, believed that this was an unprecedentedly good result in East Asia, and this was no exaggeration. China's Li Zhongsan was able to jump to 1.80 meters after only one month of training. It can be seen that China is not without talent, but it suffers from a lack of continuous practice.

(V) 100 Meters Preliminary 124

No Chinese participants. First Group: (1) Japan's Nambu Chuhei, (2) Philippines' Nepomuceno, (3) Philippines' Gandili, time: 10.9 seconds. Second Group: (1) Japan's Yoshioka Ryutoku, (2) Japan's Abu Tsurao, (3) Philippines' Isigoshi, time: 10.8 seconds.

(VI) 110 Meters Hurdles Preliminary 125

China had Lin Shaozhou and Xiao Dinghua participating. Lin was in the first group, and Xiao was in the second group. The results differed too much, and neither was selected, but both were very hardworking. (The second group's results have already been seen in the telegram and will not be repeated.)

(VII) 200 Meters Preliminary 126

China's Zhou Ende participated in the first group, and Zhong Lianji participated in the second group. Zhong Lianji was in second place at the start, but then fell back midway. In the end, Zhong gritted his teeth and desperately chased, and was not far behind the Filipino Creak in third place. The first group's time was 22.5 seconds, and the second group's was 22.1 seconds. If China's Liu Changchun had participated, there would have been hope.

(VIII) 200 Meters Low Hurdles Preliminary 127

China's Cheng Jingguan and Liang Jingping participated. Cheng was in the first group, and Liang was in the second group. Liang's score was better and was quite close to the Filipino in third place.

(IX) 400 Meters Preliminary 128

China's Liu Changchun and Zhu Ruihong participated in the first group, and Wang Jianwu and Mai Guozhen participated in the second group. Liu Changchun had a false start twice at the start. On the third start, he did not dare to move and started slower. He tried desperately to catch up but was unable to make up the difference. As a result, he only got fourth place and was eliminated. Everyone was disappointed. However, Liu had a leg injury and had not been training in Shanghai. The enemy's scores were all around 50 seconds, and Nakajima's record in the second group was even 49.4 seconds. It is no wonder that he failed.

Songjiang Boys' and Girls' 130

Middle Schools to Merge During Summer Vacation

Zhenjiang News: The Jiangsu Education Department plans to merge the Songjiang Provincial Boys' and Girls' Middle Schools during this year's summer vacation. The reasons are: (1) to save expenses; (2) to avoid dormitory disputes; (3) according to the principles for establishing senior high schools from the National Education Conference, a merger is necessary. Furthermore, because most of the female students are from Zhejiang Province, local people have criticized this, and the girls' school principal, Jiang Xuezhu, has often felt that it is difficult to handle matters. Also, because she is physically weak and often ill, she has long considered resigning. The boys' school principal, Chen Jing, was sent by the Education Department last winter to resolve the unrest. Because he is capable and handles matters effectively, he was appointed as principal. However, Chen had no intention of serving as principal and repeatedly requested to resign, but was not approved. He had to work hard to improve the school's affairs and actively reform it. Over the past half year, the results have been remarkable and deeply in line with public opinion. Now that there is a merger, Chen is considering using this opportunity to resign and return to the Education Department to fulfill his original intention. However, it is said that the authorities are extremely cautious when considering candidates for the principalship after the merger, striving to find someone who can adapt to the environment to satisfy the hopes of the local people.

Tomorrow is the May 30th Massacre Commemoration 134

A Memorial Meeting Will Be Convened

A Public Memorial Ceremony Will Be Held

Regulations Stipulated by the Municipal Propaganda Department

The May 30th Massacre was a joint slaughter of the Chinese people by British and Japanese imperialism. Recognition of and efforts to commemorate the May 30th Massacre should include: (1) The May 30th Massacre originated from the oppression of Chinese workers by Japanese-owned factories in Shanghai in February of the 14th year of the Republic of China (1925), which led to a strike. The Japanese used high-handed measures to shoot and kill the worker Gu Zhenghong, thus arousing conscious workers and patriotic students in China to participate in the Party's anti-imperialist movement. On May 30th, a grand anti-imperialist propaganda and demonstration was held in the Shanghai International Settlement. The British police chief, Englishman Everson, ordered the police to shoot and kill our patriotic unarmed civilians in a tragic scene. From May 30th to June 5th, eleven Chinese compatriots were tragically killed, eight were seriously injured, and more than a dozen were slightly injured. Subsequently, similar massacres occurred in Nanjing, Guangzhou, Jiujiang, Chongqing, and other places to support the people of Shanghai.

(2) We can draw the following conclusions by summarizing the causes and facts of the May 30th Massacre and the subsequent massacres: (1) Imperialists are united in their opposition to the Chinese National Revolutionary Movement. (2) They are at least united on the basis of this common interest. (3) Imperialists have consistently used a policy of slaughter against the Chinese National Revolutionary Movement from May 30th to the present. This is what we must deeply recognize.

(3) May 30th was a commemoration of the National Revolutionary Movement led by the Party's Premier, which directly confronted the imperialists in a bloody battle. At that time, the imperialists, seeing the awakening of the Chinese nation, could not help but panic. They did not hesitate to violate justice and humanity by using a policy of slaughter to maintain the irrational and unequal treaty rights they had obtained. However, in fact, the Chinese National Revolutionary Movement only progressed further as a result of this. The Chinese people only became more conscious and gathered under the banner of the Party. In the shortest period of time, the Northern Expedition was completed, the imperialists' henchmen were eliminated, and the foundation of the imperialists' aggressive policies in China was shaken.

(4) Since May 30th, the progress of the National Revolutionary forces in overthrowing the warlords and shaking the foundations of imperialism has increasingly proved that the imperialists' use of warlords, or the collusion of warlords with imperialists, to sabotage the progress of the revolution is doomed to failure. The failure of the traitorous officials Feng Gui, Zhang Tang, and others who colluded with imperialists last year is even more obvious. Recently, the rebellious Yan Xishan has followed in the footsteps of Feng Gui, Zhang Tang, and others to endanger the progress of the revolution and shake the foundations of the Party and the country. His failure can be foreseen. However, before he is eliminated, we must uphold the spirit of the May 30th martyrs, support the Central Government, eliminate the rebellious Yan, and forever destroy the tools used by imperialists to invade China, both old and new warlords. We must strive to abolish unequal treaties and overthrow all imperialism to complete the mission of the National Revolution.

(5) May 30th is one scene of the tragic history of the Party leading the people to resist imperialism. Therefore, to commemorate May 30th, it must be held vigorously in the places designated by the Party. We must punish all counter-revolutionary elements and communists and reorganized factions who sell out the revolution in the name of the people. We must vow to fight heroically against imperialism under the principles of the Three People's Principles. Attached slogans: (1) May 30th is the commemoration day of the imperialists' slaughter of the Chinese people. (2) Slaughtering China is the imperialists' last struggle. (3) Use the power of the National Revolution to defeat all actions of the imperialists. (4) Continue the spirit of the May 30th martyrs. (5) Overthrow all imperialism and abolish unequal treaties. (6) Protect the interests of the revolution and eliminate the remnants of warlords, Yan Xishan and Feng Yuxiang. (7) Long live the Chinese Nationalist Party. (8) Long live the Republic of China.

Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department of the Chinese Nationalist Party

The National Day of Humiliation for the Chinese people is also a revolutionary commemoration day for the Chinese people's direct resistance to the atrocities of imperialism under the oppression of the warlord government. As a result of the May 30th Massacre, the Chinese people suffered the tragedy of slaughter, but at the same time, it made the Chinese people more deeply aware that the warlords and imperialists are the sole enemies of the Chinese people. Now that the fifth anniversary of the May 30th Massacre has arrived, feudal warlords and all counter-revolutionary elements continue to attack the revolutionary rule. Recalling the martyrdom spirit of the May 30th martyrs who sacrificed themselves for the country and struggled for the people, it is truly a tragic and moving event that inspires future generations to have endless feelings of excitement. We should expand propaganda and continue the revolutionary spirit of the May 30th martyrs and the national support for the May 30th Massacre to remove all obstacles to the revolution today, consolidate the foundation of the Party and the country, and comfort the souls of the martyrs underground. Yesterday, the Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department thoroughly formulated various measures, and the probes are recorded below.

Commemoration aspects: (1) At 9:00 AM on May 30th, Party departments, agencies, organizations, and schools at all levels will send four representatives to the Penglai Grand Theater on Penglai Road in the South City of Shanghai to hold a memorial meeting. All citizens will wear black gauze armbands for one day. 5. Stop banquets and entertainment for one day.

Commemorative albums. 8. Era. 9. Other. (3) Propaganda methods: 1. Send out permanent lecture teams from each branch for propaganda. 2. Widely post slogans. 3. Distribute leaflets. 4. Publish the portraits of the May 30th martyrs and photos of the massacre in newspapers. 5. Other.

(2) Slogans: 1. May 30th is a massacre of small and weak peoples by British and Japanese imperialism. 2. May 30th is the commemoration day for the Chinese nation's resistance to the imperialists. 3. Continue the spirit of the May 30th martyrs. 4. Overthrow British and Japanese imperialism. 5. Reclaim the national concessions. 6. Eliminate the traitorous warlords Yan Xishan and Feng Yuxiang. 7. Avenge the May 30th martyrs. 8. Eliminate the Chinese Communist Party. 9. Eliminate all counter-revolutionary elements. 10. Support the Chinese Nationalist Party. 11. Implement the Three Principles of the People. 12. Complete the National Revolution. 13. Long live the Chinese Nationalist Party. 14. Long live the Republic of China.

The Three May 30th Martyrs Were Reburied in the Cemetery Yesterday 135

The coffins of the May 30th Massacre martyrs Wang Kuibao, Chen Zhaochang, and Wei Guoping were scheduled to be moved to the May 30th Cemetery yesterday. Therefore, yesterday morning, the families of the May 30th Massacre victims went to the cemetery to prepare. At 11:00 AM, the coffins of the three martyrs were first brought to the site and carried through the pre-opened door under the ladder, and the martyrs' coffins were placed in the graves. In addition to the families of Wang, Chen, and Wei who sent the coffins, no less than three or forty relatives of other deceased martyrs went to pay their respects. The quiet cemetery suddenly became lively, and the sound of wailing filled the air, making people indignant. After the burial, a solemn and grand memorial ceremony was held, and the order was as follows: (1) The families stood in front of the tomb in silence. (2) The families bowed three times to the three martyrs Wang, Chen, Wei, and other martyrs. (3) Hu Changsheng and Chen Fucai, representatives of the May 30th Massacre Victims Families Association, gave speeches on the recognition of and efforts to commemorate the May 30th Massacre. (4) Presenting flowers. (5) Reading the memorial text. (6) Reporting the circumstances of the martyrdom of the three martyrs Wang, Chen, and Wei. (7) Bowing three times to the three martyrs Wang, Chen, and Wei again. (8) The ceremony was completed. (9) Shouting slogans: The spirit of the martyrs will never die, continue the efforts of the martyrs, support the Chinese Nationalist Party, support the Families Association. The two representatives, Hu and Chen, said: Down with the demons who destroy the Families Association, reclaim the concessions, and negotiate compensation for all losses in the May 30th case.

Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, and others, chairmen of the May 30th Cemetery Board of Directors, set the date for 9:00 AM on the same day (30th) because it was the fifth anniversary of the martyrs' martyrdom. The board of directors were to be convened, and a memorial text was prepared to be presented at the Fangjia Muqiao Public Memorial Ceremony in Zhabei. The association's letter to the directors convening the public memorial is recorded below: Dear sirs, this month, the 30th is the commemoration day of the May 30th Massacre. The date for the association to hold a public memorial ceremony at the May 30th Martyrs Cemetery at 9:00 AM on that day has been set to commemorate the martyrs. Please come to the cemetery at that time to participate in the public memorial ceremony. This is a special occasion, and we wish you peace.

The Municipal Government Promulgates the Regulations of the Committee for Deliberating Rental Disputes 136

The city has mixed Chinese and foreign residents, and the number of households is increasing daily. Disputes arising from renting houses occur from time to time. In order to maintain people's livelihood and eliminate disputes, the Municipal Government invited representatives from Party departments, courts, and various agencies and organizations to formulate the Regulations of the Shanghai Special Municipal Committee for Deliberating Rental Disputes. The regulations have been approved by the National Government. It is reported that the Municipal Government has issued orders to the relevant agencies and organizations to send representatives to form a committee in accordance with the law. In addition, a public announcement was issued, and the announcement and regulations are recorded below:

Announcement by the Shanghai Special Municipal Government: For the matter of announcement, the issue of residence is one of the four major elements of people's livelihood, and it is related to the prosperity or decline of the city. The city has mixed Chinese and foreign residents, and the number of households is increasing daily. As a result, disputes arising from renting houses have also continued to occur. In order to maintain people's livelihood and eliminate disputes, the Municipal Government invited representatives from Party departments, courts, and various agencies and organizations to meet and formulate the Regulations of the Shanghai Special Municipal Committee for Deliberating Rental Disputes, which were submitted to the Executive Yuan and then approved by the National Government. In addition to publicly announcing the implementation of the regulations, orders have been issued to the relevant agencies and organizations to send representatives to form a committee in accordance with the law and convene meetings. This is a public announcement, and the regulations are recorded below for public knowledge.

Regulations: The Regulations of the Shanghai Special Municipal Committee for Deliberating Rental Disputes. Article 1: The Shanghai Special Municipal Government has established the Committee for Deliberating Rental Disputes in order to resolve disputes arising from rental relations within the city, such as termination of contracts, relocation, changes in rent, and subletting. Article 2: The committee shall be organized by the mayor's appointment and invitation of the following members, and one person shall be appointed as chairman: one representative from the Shanghai Special Municipal Government, one representative each from its affiliated Social Affairs Bureau, Land Bureau, Public Works Bureau, Public Utilities Bureau, and Public Security Bureau, one representative from the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department, one representative from the Shanghai Special Municipal Government Construction Discussion Committee, and three specialized members. Article 3: The committee shall be affiliated with the Shanghai Special Municipal Government, and its staff members shall be appointed by the Municipal Government to serve concurrently. Article 4: The members of the committee shall be unpaid, but the appointed specialized members may receive a reasonable amount of office expenses. Article 5: The committee shall not have a fixed closing date for deliberations. The chairman and members shall convene meetings at any time, but all members must be notified three days in advance. Article 6: A meeting of the committee must have more than half of the members present for deliberation, and the agreement of more than half of the members present shall be required for a resolution. If the numbers are equal, the chairman shall decide. Article 7: Upon the order of the mayor or the entrustment of the court, the committee may investigate the customary rules or common belief principles within the city regarding the resolution of general rental disputes and deliberate and decide on them, but may not violate the provisions of laws and regulations. Article 8: Regarding specific rental disputes within the city, the committee shall investigate and determine the contents of the incident and create a report for the mayor's administrative disposition or the court's judgment.

Article 9: In the event that a specific rental dispute within the city is, with the consent of both parties, ordered by the mayor to be arbitrated by the committee, or entrusted by the court for arbitration, the committee may apply the laws and regulations on civil arbitration to judge the dispute. The parties to the dispute may request the court to execute the judgment. Article 10: In the event that a specific rental dispute within the city is, at the request of one or both parties, ordered by the mayor to be mediated by the committee, or entrusted by the court for mediation, the committee may convene a meeting to deliberate and decide on the investigation method. If both parties have expressed compliance with the decision in a case ordered by the mayor for mediation, the decision shall be final. Those who should be forcibly executed may request the competent court to execute the judgment. Those who do not accept the mediation decision may request the mayor to submit the case for review by the committee within twenty days from the day after receiving the decision, but no further review may be requested after the review decision. If both parties have expressed compliance with the decision in a case entrusted by the court for mediation, the decision shall be final. Those who should be forcibly executed may request the original court to execute the judgment. Those who do not accept the mediation decision may file an objection with the original court within twenty days from the day after receiving the decision. Article 11: The determination report, judgment, or decision made by the committee at the meeting shall detail the facts, evidence, and reasons. Article 12: When investigating, arbitrating, or mediating in accordance with Articles 8 to 10 of these regulations, the committee may summon the parties to the meeting, order them to state their opinions and present evidence, and may summon witnesses to conduct an on-site inspection. If the parties fail to attend the meeting after being summoned twice, the committee may make a determination, judgment, or decision directly. Article 13: If a party to an arbitration judgment or mediation decision made by the committee has requested the court to execute the judgment, the party may apply to the court for compulsory execution in accordance with the civil execution procedure, and the court shall verify the contents and notify the Public Security Bureau to assist in the execution. Article 14: If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, the committee may propose amendments, which shall be submitted to the mayor for approval and then submitted to the National Government for approval and implementation. Article 15: These regulations shall be implemented on the date of promulgation upon approval by the National Government.

Foreign Ships Docking at Anqing Wharf 145

Ministry of Communications Has Requested Ministry of Foreign Affairs to Revoke

The Anhui Provincial Government decided to establish a public wharf in Anqing to attract foreign ships from Britain and Japan, causing great opposition from Shanghai shipping merchants. This matter was previously reported in this newspaper. It is now known that the origin of this case was a proposal from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs inspector Li Fang, stating that foreign ships on the Yangtze River could not dock in Anhui, causing inconvenience for passengers and cargo. His report made it seem as if there were no Chinese ships operating in Anqing, disregarding the fact that Sanbei Merchants Steam Navigation Co. had ships and wharfs that could facilitate the loading and unloading of cargo and passengers. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs then consulted the Anhui Provincial Government, and the Anhui Provincial Department of Construction held an enlarged meeting, deciding to establish a public wharf to attract foreign ships to avoid foreign merchants establishing wharfs inland. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company reported this matter and strongly opposed it, stating that while the Anhui Provincial Government attracting foreign ships to dock at wharfs could avoid the suspicion of establishing wharfs inland, the drawbacks would allow foreign ships to compete for inland shipping business. It also cited the third clause of the Sino-British Yantai Treaty of the Guangxu period, which prohibits foreign merchants from operating ships in the interior (Datong and Anqing in Anhui, Hukou in Jiangxi, and Wuxue, Luxikou, and Shashi in Hubei and Hunan are all inland locations and not treaty ports. According to the regulations of the Yangtze River, foreign merchants should not be allowed to load and unload goods privately. The proposed solution is to allow ships to temporarily stop and load and unload passengers and goods using civilian boats). The original clause was requested to be forwarded to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to prevent the situation. The bureau has now received a reply from the Ministry of Communications stating that it has been forwarded to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to revoke the approval for foreign ships to dock. They will notify the Anhui Provincial Government again when they receive a reply.

Ministry of Communications to Establish Wireless Communications Network 146

Settlement Method for Telegram Fees Also Drafted and Announced

Minister of Communications Wang Boqun stated that as China's news industry is developing rapidly, important communications in various places often suffer from the inability to be transmitted quickly. The reason for this is that there are many radio stations in various places, but the staff is small and insufficient to distribute the work, so they cannot immediately take photographs. After a long time, this violates the fundamental purpose of promoting the news industry. Therefore, a wireless communications network is established to ensure that messages are sent, received, and photographed as soon as they arrive, without delay. The method for settling telegram fees has also been drafted in four articles and communicated to all radio stations for compliance. The methods are as follows: (1) Wireless telegrams collected by wired telegraph offices should be sent to the radio station along with the telegram fees. (2) Telegrams received by radio stations and sent to places where no radio station is established should be sent to the local telegraph office along with the telegram fees. (3) If a telegraph office or radio station encounters obstacles due to lines, equipment, or weather and needs to transfer the telegram to another station for transmission, the telegram fee will be divided equally between the offices. (4) If a telegram received by a telegraph office or radio station cannot be sent for any reason and is transferred to the local radio station or telegraph office for transmission, the telegram fee should be handled in accordance with the collection method.

Social Bureau Investigates and Bans Rice Essence 152

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau discovered that an advertisement was published in the newspaper on May 1st regarding the sale of rice essence to solve the problem of eating. Considering that this matter concerns the health of ordinary people, personnel were sent to the Bailing Drugstore on Six Malu, east of the Central Grand Theater, which sold rice essence, to purchase a sample bottle. It was claimed that when cooking rice, adding rice essence can save rice and firewood and does not produce a stiff, burnt, or sour smell, but it is palatable and nourishing, curing diseases and saving the poor. After inspecting the instructions on the sample, there were many doubts, so the original was sent to the Health Bureau for chemical testing. The Health Bureau tested the sample and found that the alum content (17.92%) was too high and failed to prove the special effects listed in the pamphlet. It is undoubtedly a deceptive way to make money. The bureau sent a letter to the Shanghai Special District Court yesterday requesting a ban.

Local News

Huang Yihui Kidnapped 156

Two Bodyguards, One Dead and One Wounded

Chauffeur Also Injured and Died

Huang Yizhu's son, Huang Yihui, a sugar merchant from Xiamen, serves as the deputy director of the Central China Bank. One day he was kidnapped. On the day before, at dusk, he was returning home from work in his car when he was chased by two cars carrying kidnappers. As they approached Huang's car, they stopped it. Huang's two bodyguards, seeing the matter, immediately fired their guns to defend their master. The bandits also returned fire. Due to the disparity in numbers, Huang Yihui was kidnapped. One of the bodyguards was killed and the other was injured. The chauffeur, injured in the abdomen, also died in the hospital. This newspaper learned the details that night, but did not publish them immediately for other reasons. Although Huang is a sugar tycoon, his situation is far from what it used to be due to the influence of the sugar industry. Huang Yihui personally only has a small amount of household expenses provided by his father, and his education is very strict. Therefore, the actual situation is not wealthy. Huang Yizhu is currently suffering from madness and resting at home.

Kidnapping Details: Huang Yihui is 34 years old and lives at 22 Baojian Road. At 6 PM the day before yesterday, after finishing his work, he took his own Stutz Bearcat automobile number 824, driven by the driver Yu Yongcai. Inside the car, in addition to Huang, were bodyguards Wu Xiying and Ma Ping'an, each carrying a pistol to protect the car. When they reached Haig Road, they noticed two cars following them. When they reached 346 Haig Road, a motorcycle suddenly overtook Huang's car from the left. The driver, Yu Yongcai, fearing a collision, slowed down to let it pass. At this time, the two cars behind had approached Huang's car and stopped abruptly. Four kidnappers jumped out, each holding a pistol, and opened the door to fire at the bandits, totaling five shots. Unfortunately, none of them hit. The bandits returned fire, hitting bodyguard Wu Xiying, who fell to the ground and died. Ma Ping'an was also injured and unable to resist. The chauffeur, Yu Yongcai, was injured in the waist and could not resist. At this time, Huang Yihui sat motionless in the car, his face pale, and was forced into the bandits' car, which sped away. The time was 6:20 PM. When the Jing'an Temple police heard the news, they ordered a large group of Chinese and foreign detectives to drive to the scene, but it was already 7:00 PM. The bandits had gone far and could not be pursued. In addition to finding bullet casings and broken glass on the ground, they sent Ma and Yu to the Red Cross Hospital on Haig Road for treatment. Ma's injuries were light and he could be saved, but Yu's injuries were fatal and he died after Wu. The detectives carried the bodies of Wu and Yu to the forensic examination office on Fellen Road. The two sides exchanged fire no less than twenty times. One of the bandits was injured in the leg and carried onto the car by the bandits, who calmly escaped. It was also heard that the motorcycle had been following Huang Yihui for several weeks.

Forensic Examination by the Court: At 10:00 AM yesterday, Guo Huaipu, the prosecutor commissioned by the Special District Local Court, arrived at the site for forensic examination. He took the public seat and reported that he had gone to the scene to investigate after receiving the report, saying that he had found several bullet casings, which have been handed over to the firearms examination office for examination. Subsequently, Wu, the wife of the deceased Yu Yongcai, claimed that she was from Ningbo and currently lived at 162 Huanlong Road. My husband was tragically shot and killed, leaving behind three children and an elderly mother. The family is already poor, and the livelihood will be even more difficult in the future. She requested that the murderers be arrested and justice be served, and requested the bank to provide compensation. In addition, Guan, the wife of the deceased Wu Xiying, claimed that she was from Beijing, 29 years old, and had parents-in-law and children who depended on her husband for support. She requested that the murderers be arrested and punished, and requested the bank to provide compensation. Prosecutor Guo subsequently instructed Yu and Guan to take Yu Yongcai and Wu Xiying's bodies away for coffin burial, and ordered the Central China Bank to pay 400 yuan in compensation to each family. He also ordered the police to strictly arrest the murderers and bring them to justice.

Hen Repeatedly Lays Strange Eggs 157

Two Hens Lay Three Strange Eggs

Eggs Inside Eggs, Peculiar Shape

Some Think It's a Sign of Wealth

Rice Shop Owner Very Happy

Chen Longxing Rice Shop in the West End of Tangqiao Town, Pudong, is owned by a man named Chen (commonly known as "Little Uncle") from Jiangbei. He raises a hen for eggs and food. In July of last year, the hen suddenly laid a strange egg, about one foot and three inches long and four inches in circumference, slightly larger than a normal goose egg. After the shop owner broke it open, there was an egg inside, the size of a normal hen's egg. For a time, it was rumored to be a great wonder in the neighborhood, and people came to see it. They all said that they had seen double-yolk eggs, but never an egg inside an egg, and they all praised it as a miracle. This strange news was published in this newspaper last year. Soon after the strange egg was laid, the hen was stolen, and a relative of the shop owner brought a black hen from Jiangbei and gave it to the shop to raise. Recently, within a week, it also laid a strange egg, which was even larger than the strange egg laid by the other hen last year, and the shell was also hard. After falling to the ground, it broke immediately, and the yolk and white were all there. The strangest thing was that there was another egg next to the yolk, also hard-shelled and the size of a normal hen's egg. The shop owner was indescribably happy that the hen had laid an egg inside an egg twice, and immediately put the strange egg in a bowl, treating it as a treasure for people to see. Therefore, the shop was often crowded with people watching. Unexpectedly, the hen laid another egg the morning before, with an even stranger shape, round and not long, different from the previous egg, with a circumference of about one foot, five or six inches, like a ball or a tangerine. The outer shell was also hard, and it broke immediately when it fell to the ground due to its weight. In addition to the yolk and white, there was also a hard-shelled small egg the size of a normal hen's egg inside. The shop owner immediately moved it to a bowl and did not cook it with the previous long egg. It is still in the shop. People who heard the news and came to see it were constant. Some superstitious people even said that the shop had laid three strange eggs in a row, which was a sign of wealth. Those who heard this laughed. However, those with deeper knowledge said that it is not surprising that hens lay eggs with double yolks, but it is rare for them to lay two eggs in a row. Now, with a large egg surrounding another egg at the same time, I don't know how the chicken's stomach is constructed. It is worth studying. However, it must have felt very distressed when laying it. The situation is recorded here for the reference of physiologists.

The Second Normal School Alumni Association Inaugural Meeting 160

The graduates of the former Jiangsu Provincial Second Normal School, now in their fourteenth class, have been serving in various regions and have had little contact. The 28th of this month marks the 25th anniversary of the Second Normal School. Yesterday afternoon at 6:00 PM, alumni of the school gathered at the Jinlong Western Restaurant for a commemorative dinner. Over 200 alumni from both local and out-of-town locations attended the memorial ceremony to establish an alumni association. Representatives at all levels were elected on the spot to be responsible for the association's affairs.

Articles of Association of the Jiangsu Provincial Second Normal School Alumni Association (Chapter 1) General Principles Article 1: The name of this association is the Jiangsu Provincial Third Normal School Alumni Association. Article 2: The purpose of this association is to promote friendship, improve education, and manifest the spirit of revolution. (Chapter 2) Membership Article 3: The qualifications for membership are as follows: (A) Graduates of this school (B) Faculty and staff of this school Article 4: The obligations of members are as follows: (A) Abide by the constitution of this association (B) Abide by the resolutions of this association (C) Pay membership dues (D) Overthrow academic cliques and eliminate all evil forces Article 5: The rights of members are as follows: (A) The right to vote and be elected (B) The right to enjoy and use the facilities of this association (C) The right to entrust this association to introduce employment opportunities (D) The right to receive publications of this association (Chapter 3) Organization

Article 6: The highest authority of this association is the General Membership Meeting. During the adjournment of the General Membership Meeting, the Representative Assembly is the highest authority. During the session of the Representative Assembly, the Executive Committee is the highest authority. Article 7: If members of this association wish to organize branches in various regions, they must obtain the approval of this association. The detailed rules for their organization shall be determined by the Representative Assembly. (Chapter 4) General Membership Meeting Article 8: The General Membership Meeting shall be held once a year on the school anniversary. However, an extraordinary General Membership Meeting may be convened if the Representative Assembly deems it necessary or if requested by more than one-third of the members. (D) Implement all resolutions of the General Membership Meeting or the Representative Assembly. (E) Submit proposals to the General Membership Meeting or the Representative Assembly. (F) Have the right to attend the Representative Assembly and speak at the Representative Assembly, but without the right to vote. Article 21: The detailed rules of the Executive Committee shall be determined by the Executive Committee itself. Article 22: The detailed rules of the Standing Committee shall be determined by the Executive Committee. Article 23: The detailed rules of the Special Committee shall be determined by the Executive Committee. (Chapter 7) Funding Article 24: The annual expenses of this association shall be borne by all members and may be subsidized by the school. Article 25: Members shall pay annual dues of one yuan, which shall be paid at the general meeting. Article 26: In the event of special circumstances, the Executive Committee may decide to raise special donations. (Chapter 8) Supplementary Provisions Article 27: If there are any inappropriate provisions in the constitution of this association, they may be amended by the General Membership Meeting and the Representative Assembly. Article 28: The constitution of this association shall come into effect from the date of its adoption.

Seven Sand Boats Robbed 161

Around 8:00 PM the night before, a large number of sand boats were sailing through the waters of Sheshan Honggang, more than a hundred miles outside the Wusong estuary. Suddenly, twenty or thirty Ningbo boats swarmed in, filled with over two hundred pirates. They blocked the passage and boarded the sand boats, forcing them to sail forward with the pirate ships. The ships that were robbed included the Jin Yutai and Lu Yongmao from Liuhe, the Gao Changmao and Fu Changmao from Shijiusuo, the Jin Yuanlai and Gongdeshun from Shandong, and the Lu Yuanmao from Chongming, totaling seven large sand boats. They were sailed to the vicinity of Lvsi Town, where the pirates released all the crew members, instructing them to go to Shanghai, prepare the ransom, and report the news. It was learned yesterday that the Gongdeshun and Jin Yuanlai, two of the robbed ships, were export sand boats and were not carrying goods, so their value was relatively low. The ship owners had already paid 2,800 yuan to redeem them. There has been no news about the remaining ships since they were robbed.

Establishment of the Shanghai Special Municipality Chinese Cigarette Factory Trade Association 164

Since being ordered to reorganize, the preparatory work for the Shanghai Special Municipality Chinese Cigarette Factory Trade Association has been completed. Yesterday, the official inaugural meeting was held at the Business Consolidation Association on Beihe Commercial Road, with over 50 people in attendance. The meeting began at 3:00 PM with formal ceremonies. Chairman Wu Tingsheng reported on the reorganization process, stating that although the Chinese cigarette industry has a 30-year history, it has never had a practical organization. Under the oppression of imperialism, it has been difficult to develop. Therefore, even with alliances, there has been little significant effect. Last year, Lao Jingxiu, Dai Gengxin, Hong Cangting, and others, recognizing this, proposed to gather most of the industry to unite and organize a trade association. During this process, they encountered many difficulties. Fortunately, all members of the industry felt that unity was necessary to resist foreign insults and resolve aggression. Therefore, they actively participated and supported, resulting in today's situation. Now, under the guidance of party and government organs and higher-level organizations, the inaugural meeting is being held today. The gathering of industry members demonstrates a spirit of struggle. He hoped that all comrades would continue to work tirelessly to solve various difficulties with their own strength and fight a decisive battle with foreign merchants, so that the dying Chinese tobacco industry could find a savior and not let down the enthusiasm of the three representatives who came to guide them. He personally felt particularly gratified. As for the association's charter, which was once adopted, it should be reread and amended because half a year has passed and it may be forgotten or inappropriate. Next, the general meeting charter was passed. The chairman read each article, and there were no objections. The chairman stated that the charter was approved internally. Compared with the industrial and commercial trade association charter issued by the Business Consolidation Association, there were shortcomings that needed to be amended by two representatives. Then, it would be submitted to the Business Consolidation Association for approval and implementation. All attending representatives approved, and Yao Jixian and Bao Gengsheng were elected to handle the matter. There were no other objections. Next, the executive committee was elected. The results were Wu Tingsheng, Lao Jingxiu, Shen Yankang, Hong Cangting, Bao Gengsheng, Dai Gengxin, Yu Banqin, Yao Jixian, Sun Xingde, Yao Weixiong, Wang Qiuchan, Zhang Xinliang, Jiang Lanting, Li Xuedong, and Jiang Pinyu, 15 people elected as executive committee members. Next, most of the alternates were Sun Lishan and Wang Yunfu. Next, the executive committee members were sworn into office. Next, Li Yongxiang, a representative of the Civil Training Association, gave a training speech, stating that all of you are leaders in the tobacco industry and probably know the meaning of organizing a trade association: one is for commercial interests, and the other is for the national economy and the people's livelihood. I also know the current painful and declining situation of cigarette factories. The first reason is that Chinese merchants lack the ability to compete due to the economic aggression of imperialism, and the remaining domestic rebels have not been pacified, and the government has not been able to wholeheartedly protect industry, which is also a pain point for Chinese merchants. There are many other reasons. The only solution now is to unite and assist the country to achieve freedom and equality internationally, and to effectively abolish all unequal treaties, which is how you can solve your own pain. At that time, there will be various good methods to make Chinese factories develop every day. The ultimate goal is to prevent foreign goods from being sold in China. This is the meaning of organizing a trade association. Then, the executive committee held its first executive committee meeting and elected Wu Tingsheng, Lao Jingxiu, Bao Gengsheng, Yao Jixian, and Shen Xingde as standing committee members. The meeting adjourned after 6:00 PM.

A Lawsuit for Breach of Marriage Arising from Tea Money 165

Jin Renyuan, a 23-year-old from Baoshan, residing at No. 50, Sangyuan Street, outside the Dananmen, engaged Luo Runlian's daughter, Xiuying, of No. 591, Daji Road, outside the Ximen, on April 3rd of the 16th year of the Republic of China, through matchmakers Wang Genlin and Jin Abing. At that time, it was stated that the tea money would be 200 yuan and two sets of clothes. At the time of the engagement, 100 yuan in silver dollars was sent in advance, along with 6 yuan for fruit and a pair of gold rings, a gold hairpin, a gold-plated soft bracelet, and a gold-plated Ruyi hairpin (the gold hairpin was returned at the time because it was deemed too small, and the man's family was asked to exchange it). A date was chosen for the wedding this autumn, and the man's family notified the woman's family in advance. However, the woman's family stated that the remaining 100 yuan of tea money should also be sent as soon as possible in order to purchase all the dowry items. However, the man's family denied that the tea money was 200 yuan and filed a lawsuit with the local court, claiming that the fiancee's father, Luo Runlian, intended to breach the marriage and requesting that the marriage contract be upheld. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wang Qufei held a hearing. The plaintiff, Jin Renyuan, stated the previous situation and claimed that when the engagement was made, he had paid 106 yuan in tea money in full. Now, they suddenly claim that they still need 100 yuan in tea money and two sets of clothes, which he was really unable to afford. According to the matchmaker witnesses, Wang Chenshi (Wang Genlin's mother) and Jin Chenshi (Jin Abing's wife), the tea money was actually 200 yuan. It was stated that 100 yuan in silver dollars would be taken at the time of the engagement, and another 100 yuan would be taken at the time of the wedding. The jewelry was two gold pieces and two silver pieces. According to Luo Wangshi, 38 years old, from Nantong, Xiuying is my daughter. It was stated at the time that the tea money was 200 yuan and two sets of clothes. The judge obtained the statements and mediated the case in court, ordering the plaintiff to pay 80 yuan in tea money and two sets of clothes. The plaintiff replied that he had no money and could not agree. The judge said that these clothes are for your wife to wear, and even if you were asked to pay for three or four sets, you should do it. Moreover, the defendant's side does not object to the marriage. You should not rashly file a lawsuit. He repeatedly persuaded the plaintiff, but the plaintiff insisted that he had no money. Therefore, the mediation failed, and after a debate, it was considered concluded and set for judgment on the 31st of this month.

Husband Contracts Syphilis, Wife Files for Divorce 167

Huang Ayin, a young woman from Ningbo, had no one to rely on after her husband's death. However, after Ayin married into the family, Jiufa became lazy and was laid off. The daily expenses of the family depended entirely on Ayin's work. Last winter, Jiufa visited a prostitute outside and contracted syphilis, which was then transmitted to Ayin. As a result, quarrels arose frequently in the family. Now, Huang Ayin has hired lawyer Chen Wenxiang to file a lawsuit for divorce in the local court, citing reasons such as failure to provide support and transmission of syphilis. After being ordered to summon them, the trial judge instructed both parties to go to the hospital to identify whether they had syphilis in order to make a decision. Yesterday morning, Presiding Judge Guo Shouyi held another hearing. Both parties complied with the summons and appeared in court. The defendant also hired lawyer Zhu Honglie to appear in court. The judge briefly questioned both parties and said to the defendant, Fu Jiufa, "Your syphilis is very deep, and a doctor has already identified it. Moreover, Huang Ayin's syphilis is also quite severe. However, was Ayin's syphilis transmitted by you?" He replied, "I have a hernia, not syphilis sores. Ayin's syphilis started this spring." At this point, the plaintiff said, "My sores were transmitted to me by him last November." The judge said, "Why didn't you report it at that time?" She replied, "I thought it would get better, but I didn't expect it to not heal even now." The judge then invited Prosecutor Li Gongchen to the court to express his opinion. The lawyers for both parties then made their statements. The plaintiff requested a divorce, while the defendant agreed to the divorce but wanted compensation for the wedding gifts, banquet expenses, and other losses, totaling 400 yuan. The judge then announced that the debate was concluded and the judgment would be announced later.

Qiping Tobacco Factory Evades Taxes 173

Sued by the Cigarette Tax Bureau

Please Compensate for More Than Ten Thousand Silver Dollars in Taxes

The Qiping Tobacco Factory at No. 558, Wanxingfang, Xinji浜 Road, Hongkou, is equipped with a cigarette-making machine owned by Zheng Xiang and employs over 20 workers. It produces and sells cigarettes privately every day and never adheres to the stamping requirements. In January of this year, the Jiangsu Cigarette Tax Bureau discovered the tax evasion. Director Tang ordered investigators to cooperate with the Harbin Police Station to dispatch detectives to the Qiping Tobacco Factory, where they found two boxes of unstamped cigarettes, each containing 50,000 cigarettes. According to the stamp tax regulations, a fine of 30 times the amount should be imposed. If the fine is not paid, the cigarettes will be confiscated. Factory owner Zheng Xiang did not comply with the regulations and pay the fine. Therefore, the Bureau ordered that all the seized cigarettes be confiscated and sued Zheng in the Special District Local Court for tax evasion, which harmed national revenue and required compensation to prevent imitation. They requested that Zheng Xiang be summoned to court to be ordered to pay 17,550 silver dollars in taxes. The calculation method is based on the period from April of last year to the date of the discovery, a total of ten months, all of which were tax evasion periods. The minimum daily output of cigarettes was two boxes, each containing 50,000 cigarettes. The stamp tax for seventh-grade cigarettes should be 1,755 silver dollars per month, accumulating to the above amount in ten months. The court repeatedly issued summonses, but the defendant Zheng Xiang never appeared. The Qiping Tobacco Factory is now managed by a Japanese person. Yesterday morning, the court held another hearing. Because the defendant was absent, the presiding judge, Yang Yi, appointed a special agent for defense. The lawyer for the plaintiff, the Cigarette Tax Bureau, first stated the facts of the case, presented various evidence, and stated that the factory was indeed opened by Zheng Xiang. Although it is now managed by a Japanese person, this is a private transfer after the incident occurred. The plaintiff cannot recognize this and should request a judgment ordering compensation in full to emphasize national taxes. The lawyer for the defendant then made a defense. Judge Yang Yi announced that the judgment would be announced on the morning of the 31st of this month.

Wu Dongsheng's Tragic Suicide by Hanging 180

Wife and Lover

Adulterer Becomes the Undertaker

Wu Dongsheng, a native of Wuxi, was forty-five years old. He used to make a living farming in his hometown. His wife, Zhu, is currently forty-three years old and has two daughters and one son, all of whom have grown up. In the tenth year of the Republic (1921), Zhu, because she was idle and did not engage in proper business, became involved with Wang Jifa, a fellow villager. Not long after, she secretly fled with her two daughters and son to Shanghai, where she cohabitated with Wang at No. 41, Xihuaqin Fang, Bailinan Road, in western Shanghai. They opened a boarding house to make a living. The second daughter is already married to a Mr. Huang, and the son is also in school. Only the eldest daughter stays at home to help with household chores. The family is reunited and is quite well-off. Unexpectedly, Wu Dongsheng had been unemployed in his hometown for a long time and was struggling to make a living. At the beginning of March this year, he came to Shanghai directly to his wife's place and saw that his children had grown up and Wang and Zhu were living as husband and wife, like a magpie occupying a dove's nest. Unable to reverse the situation, he was extremely depressed. He was addicted to opium and needed six or seven small oceans a day. Although his wife provided him with a little every day, it was never enough to satisfy him, and she often complained. Wu tolerated it and temporarily stayed. Suddenly, at about 5:30 AM yesterday morning, Wu took advantage of everyone being asleep, untied his belt, and hanged himself. By the time the others realized it, he had already died. Officer Wei of the Third Police Station of the Sixth District learned of the incident and immediately led the police to investigate. He arrested the lover, Wang Jifa, the deceased's wife, Zhu, and the three children and took them to the Sixth District Police Station. District Chief Ren interrogated them separately. According to the lover, Wang Jifa, thirty-nine years old, from Wuxi, who runs a boarding house, has been involved with Zhu for ten years and has two daughters. Zhu stated that she was forty-three years old and that because her parents had no sons, they had recruited Wu Dongsheng as her husband. She got married when she was seventeen and had two daughters and one son. Later, Wu did not engage in proper business and had a difficult life, so she became involved with Wang and has been cohabitating with him for ten years. She also has two daughters with Wang. She came to Shanghai with Wang five years ago. After Wu came to Shanghai at the beginning of March, she still provided him with food and opium. She did not know that he would suddenly commit suicide. According to the eldest daughter, A Rong, nineteen years old, currently stays at home. The second daughter, Huang Wu, is eighteen years old and lives at Peichang Hardware Store on Beishansi Road. The son, Gen Da, is sixteen years old and is currently in school. After District Chief Ren took the statements, he immediately prepared a document and transferred them to the court for interrogation. He also ordered the local bailiff, Zhao Hefu, to report to the local court and request them to send someone for an autopsy. At 2:00 PM, the court appointed Prosecutor Yang Wenjun and Clerk Mao Zhenxin, along with an autopsy official, to come to the scene for an autopsy. They found that the deceased had indeed died by hanging and ordered the family to sign a guarantee to claim the body for coffin burial.

Revised Regulations of the Directorate General of Posts 184

Postal Workers' Unions

Raise Four Key Points

Telegraph to the Legislative Yuan

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union and the Postal Employees' Union sent a telegram to President Hu of the Legislative Yuan and the Legislative Committee regarding the change of the Postal Administration to the Postal Directorate General and the revision of the regulations, saying: (Titles omitted) "We recently read in the newspaper that the Postal Administration has been changed to the Postal Directorate General and that the revised regulations have been sent to your esteemed Yuan for review. We believe that the revision of the Directorate General's regulations is closely related to the colleagues of the unions and has a profound impact on the future of the postal service. However, because we are unable to know the details of the revision, we dare not rashly offer our suggestions. However, based on our limited views, there are several matters that are crucial and cannot be ignored. We are specially submitting them for your consideration and adoption: (1) The personnel system of the post office should be maintained. The postal service's personnel system, which requires examinations, is a fundamental measure for ensuring integrity. The appointments, promotions, and demotions are all regulated, allowing employees at all levels to serve with peace of mind, which is necessary to maintain. (2) The finances of the post office should be clearly separated from the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau. According to accounting principles, each organization should have its own independent and complete accounting system, which should not be intertwined with each other. This will allow the financial increases and decreases of each organization to be clearly understood, and competition with each other will not be able to rely on the state-owned enterprise, which will allow for the hope of development. The clear separation of the finances of the two bureaus is urgent. (3) The postal economy should be absolutely transparent. The transparency of the economy has always been advocated by our party, because secret financial management can easily lead to corruption and confusion. In the postal service, postal workers do not understand the true economic situation, and all kinds of demands arise from this, which is also a source of disputes. Economic transparency can eliminate malpractice and cannot be ignored. (4) All post office staff, from the director general downwards, should be selected from within the bureau. The position of director general is extremely important and is related to the national postal facilities. If an outsider who does not understand postal affairs is appointed, there will be many obstacles. The regulations of the Postal Directorate General promulgated by the National Government when it established its capital in Nanjing originally had this provision, which shows that the policy is not easy to change and is pertinent. However, due to the private convenience of one or two people, they did not hesitate to request changes. Now, it is urgent to restore it to remedy the situation. All of these points are clearly limited in scope and may have already been stipulated in the regulations or will be revised by your esteemed Yuan, so there is no need for us to worry about them. However, because these matters are of great importance, we are submitting this document to your esteemed Yuan for your consideration and adoption. The future of the postal service depends on it. We are at your command. Shanghai Postal Workers' Union, Shanghai Postal Employees' Union."

Letter from the Pharmaceutical Workers' Union to the Capital's Petition Representatives 185

The Pharmaceutical Workers' Union sent a letter to the Capital's Petition Representatives, saying: "Respectfully to Mr. Chen Qiaqing, Wang Yansong, Wen Lanting, Ye Huijun, and Wang Xiaolai: We have learned from the newspapers that you have been entrusted with the important task of the Chamber of Commerce and have been elected as the petition representatives of the capital for our industry. You will soon go to Beijing to request the central government to withdraw its decision to resolve the disputes in our industry. We believe that you are well-known figures in Shanghai and have a reputation throughout the country. It is not something that you would do to be tempted and incited by the Pharmaceutical Industry Association, leading to the loss of your reputation. We dare not be presumptuous and respectfully state to you that the origin and end of the disputes in our industry are known to everyone, and the right and wrong are clear to public opinion. The Pharmaceutical Industry Association has run out of arguments and has repeatedly petitioned the central government three times, all of which have been rejected. It should not be difficult to submit to the order, but because of its heavy selfishness, it stubbornly resists and ignores the principles of law, humanity, and reason, forming the current stalemate. How should the central figures of society mediate in order to quell the storm? However, you are persuaded by the association to be willing to be pioneers, ignoring the orders of the central government, not speaking out for justice, only seeking unilateral benefits, and not hesitating to create a false impression, invisibly raising the emotions of class struggle. Regardless of the outcome of the petition, it goes without saying that you will be abandoned by the public and rejected by your compatriots. Wise and benevolent people will definitely not do this. Moreover, the central government's decision is impartial and fair, and it has sincere intentions. Our party is the leader representing the whole country. If it is as the association says, 'forced,' then the party will lose its purpose. This is also something that you would deny. Before you were appointed, our union deeply hoped that the representatives could uphold justice and transform their stubbornness. We did not expect that you would volunteer to go against justice. Now, reading the opinions expressed by the representatives in today's newspaper, it is truly shocking. Enlightened people like you should not be like this. Moreover, the representatives are either giants in the business world or famous figures of the time. They must be able to uphold the intentions of the party and sympathize with the suffering of the people, and conform to the will of the people. Therefore, our union does not avoid the risk of being punished and dares to offer frank advice. We will take the blame for our faults. If you are willing to accept our sincere words, we will be grateful. Respectfully wishing you good health."

Continued Record of Jishenghui's Emergency Relief in Huaiyin 186

The China Jishenghui previously learned that the famine in Xiba and other places in Huaiyin County, Jiangsu Province, was extremely severe. The Jishenghui and the Suzhou Relief Society jointly allocated 5,000 yuan, and the branch association raised 1,000 yuan on its own, totaling 6,000 yuan, which was remitted to the relief director, Zhou Yuan Kai, to distribute with his friends. This has already been reported in the newspapers. Now, the association has repeatedly received letters from Director Zhou stating that the laborers and the elderly and weak in Xiba cannot get enough to eat every day and cannot survive without relief. Yesterday, the association telegraphed Director Zhou to increase the relief by 2,000 yuan, which has already been cashed and remitted for use. It also informed him that only those who are extremely poor and helpless and cannot survive without relief should be given additional relief in order to ensure that the funds are not wasted and the results are practical, which is in line with the association's purpose of providing on-site disaster relief and saving lives. There are disasters everywhere in our country, and relief is unsustainable. How can people with the heart to help come forward to save the catastrophe in case it happens?

Record of the Executive Committee of the Ciyouhui 187

On the 24th of this month, the Executive Committee of the China Ciyou Xieji Association held a meeting at the Guohuo Bank. The meeting was presided over by Chairman Kong Yongzhi. The National Walking Group's Commemorative Album Will Be Published 188

Since its departure, the National Walking Group has established a Shanghai office temporarily located within the National Road Construction Association on Route Père Robert, French Concession. It has repeatedly received letters from people in distant places inquiring about the content of the commemorative album that has been compiled and prepared for several months. It has now been completed and printed in 10,000 copies on 100-pound, 16-open Dowling paper to be distributed to people throughout the country. The cover features the title by Shanghai's great calligrapher and painter, Wang Yiting, and the departure photos taken by Mr. Hu Boxiang and Mr. Guo Xiqi, which are printed in a two-color set of editions. The content includes the insightful comments and great works of more than ten gentlemen, including Yu Youren, Chu Minyi, Zheng Hongzha, and Ye Gongchuo, as well as the comments of the press. Each article includes a portrait of the author. Mr. Pan Yangyao, the mentor of the group, added a preface, the origin of the walking group, an outline of the declaration, portraits and short histories of the members, the walking plan, and the route, totaling tens of thousands of words, all of which are extremely valuable and important. The front page features the certificate of the National Government and the instructions of various departments. The middle pages feature Mr. Hu Boxiang's paintings and Ambassador Wang Jingqi's farewell poems, which are exquisitely printed on copperplate paper and are extremely valuable. It is said that it has already been printed and will be published soon. The commemorative album is not for sale and it is said that you only need to pay 30 cents in postage to receive a copy. It is also reported that the group has now safely arrived in Qingjiang and will stay there for a while before heading to Lianshui, Xin'an Town, Dayishan, and Guanyun County to stay at Dengyuntai Mountain to sort out the work in Jiangsu.
