Free Talk

To Be Dismissed With A Smile 191

Philanthropist (consoling a wounded soldier in a hospital while distributing fruit)丨Poor man, haven't you lost a leg?

Soldier丨Yes, it was blown off by a cannonball while attacking the enemy's fort.

Female philanthropist (giving him an apple)丨Oh, poor man, please have an apple.

Soldier丨Thank you. Next time, if I lose another leg, then please give me an orange.

Judge丨You say your purse was stolen by him, is that true?

Victim丨Absolutely true.

Thief丨He's lying, I didn't steal it.

Judge丨Do you remember how much money was in the purse?

Victim丨I remember, there were twenty-four silver dollars.

Thief丨He's lying again, it was really twenty-five dollars.

A丨You cried when you read a tragic novel, but yesterday a painting also made me cry a lot.

B丨Is the theme of that painting very sad?

A丨No, it was actually a large nude beauty painting. I was standing there absorbed in looking at it when the rope broke and the frame hit me on the head, making me cry in pain.

A丨Does your watchdog bite people?

B丨We just bought it today, and we don't know if it bites or not. We're just looking for a stranger to try it out on. Would you be willing to help?

Anecdotes of Gu Heyi by Zheng Yimei 192

Gu Heyi, the wine offering official of the painting academy, has passed away in Wuzhong. Heyi was the son of Fangbo of Zishan. Zishan managed a separate residence in Hulong Street called Yiyuan, and every pavilion, hall, studio, and house collected Song Dynasty poetry as couplets, which were exquisite and cleverly matched, and were passed down by word of mouth. Heyi relied on the legacy of his ancestors to devote himself to painting, and his landscape paintings were as famous as those of Lu Lianfu. The price was remarkably high. His sworn brother, Zhao Mianyun, once begged for a fan painting for forty gold and a small painting for a hundred gold, but the essence was condensed and refined, which was indeed different from ordinary works. There are many counterfeit works on the outside. Some people asked him to investigate, and Heyi laughed and thanked them, saying: There are many discerning eyes in the world, and the authenticity is naturally different. However, his own works are also difficult to avoid being crude. If the crude ones are attributed to counterfeit works, wouldn't that be okay? Heyi was not good at inscriptions, and the title of the painting often came from the hand of Mr. Someone from the Western seat. Mr. Someone was a famous and talented scholar who was known in Wuzhong. Heyi and Zhao Yunhe were good friends. Yunhe once showed Heyi one or two of his 100 books, and Heyi praised them greatly and wanted to ask for one. Yunhe promised to give him a refined work later. Unexpectedly, Heyi fell ill and never recovered. Yunhe heard the news and called out for shame. At that time, his liver yang disease broke out, and he rushed to Wuzhong to pay his respects and burn the paintings in front of the spirit to fulfill his previous agreement. Heyi loved peaches. Wu Ziding, a fellow traveler, asked him to paint the Bamboo Island Tears Picture for several years without success. Last summer, he specially asked a friend from Fenghua to buy a basket of giant peaches and brought them to him to urge him to complete it, but he repeatedly delayed it. The throwing of peaches to repay jade only became an empty wish. It turned out that Heyi's hands had been trembling in recent years, and this spring he suffered a stroke and his limbs were not working properly. It was not because he cherished his ink. Recently, Heyi has opened a separate residence in Zhujia Garden, where he died of illness. His sons and nephews are all from the same family and are famous for their paintings. His eldest son, Gongxiong, was my classmate at Caoqiao School and was very close to me. Heyi's name is Linshi, his style name is Xijin, and Heyi is his other name.

Record of Being Ordered to Transport Horses by Qiulang 193

My friend, Mr. Tang, works as a quartermaster in the 9th Division of the Hankou Army. We were happy to see each other, but Mr. Tang came here to receive horses and transport them to the front line to help in the war. Later, I visited him in the hotel, but I did not have the opportunity to express my feelings because he was in a hurry to leave, with no time to warm his seat. However, I also admire his courage to serve the public. There was also a medical officer Meng from the 6th Division in the same room. When asked, he was also ordered to receive horses, so they could help each other and things were more convenient.

Yang Yixiao's Tale of Mount Rufeng's Milk Spring 194

A woman's two breasts are tall and protruding, hence the name Mount Rufeng (Breast Peak). Seventy miles southwest of the county seat, the central peak is like a lid, and the twelve ridges on the east and west sides arch towards the north of the city. There is a Baoshen Cave on the cliff that is ten feet deep. The spring flows like milk, sweet and drinkable. However, although human milk is sweet, people with damp and hot bodies have yellow breast milk. Cow's milk is hot in nature, and horse's milk is cold. If the spring flows like milk, the taste is sweet and the color is white, and it is neither cold nor hot. Men, women, old, and young can drink it at any time of the year. Regular drinking of the spring milk from Mount Rufeng can also strengthen the body.

In addition to Meng Jun contacting the authorities in the concession to arrange for staff to assist in the loading and unloading of horses at the wharf and the South Railway Station, Tang Jun also rushed to the Sixth District to ask the District Chief to recruit dozens of laborers to facilitate the management of feed and other matters along the way. He also hired service soldiers to go to the South City to purchase thousands of bags of wheat bran to feed the horses. It is necessary to load them immediately, drive the car through Beijing, and transfer them to the front line for use. According to Mr. Tang, the division has been victorious in all battles since its departure, and the vanguard has already passed Lanfeng, etc. He also said that Jiang Dingwen, the commander of the 9th Division and the commander-in-chief of the right wing, is brave and loyal and has repeatedly made meritorious service. He is especially able to share weal and woe with his subordinates, so the officers and soldiers all respect him. I think that when the horses are sent to the front line, they will further strengthen the morale of the army, and the famous generals and good steeds will soon be able to report victory.

A Record of the Acrobatic Skills of the Huiluo Circus by Cheng Zhizheng 195

Last April, the Harmsdun Circus came to Shanghai and showed its acrobatic skills to entertain us. Its great and novel performances still left a great impression on the people of Shanghai. The Huiluo Circus has come to Shanghai again, and the performance site is also located at the original site on Route Bayard. As a result, as soon as it was publicized, it attracted the attention of many people. Yesterday was the first performance of the group. I went to watch the afternoon show with my friend and briefly recorded the special features that Harmsdun did not have for the readers.

Female Strongman The first performer was a trapeze artist, whose mind-boggling movements were as unique as those of the Harmsdun group. The difference was that the performer in this group was a woman. The woman's body was extremely strong and the abundance of her muscles was amazing. When performing, she inverted her body and tossed a child to the other side, with agile techniques. The audience was amazed and applauded a lot.

Bicycle on a Tightrope Walking on a tightrope is not surprising, but riding a bicycle on a tightrope has never been seen before. The performer that day was a young girl with a dark face, produced in Africa. Her technique can be called unsurpassed. Some say that the wheels of the bicycle are specially made with a concave shape, but it is not easy.

Living Under the Knife Then, a huge wooden board came out, with a girl standing with her back to it. Another girl threw sharp knives at the board. All the knives stood upright next to the child's body, with no room for a hair. If it deviated slightly, it would be unimaginable. Later, with the handle of the knife tied with a torch, she still threw it as before. The fire was raging near the girl's body, which made people dare not watch. This kind of acrobatics is rare.

The Humor of Dwarfs There was a dwarf in the group with a height of only two feet. He was dressed in a formal suit and had an imposing manner. He performed various humorous programs, and the audience laughed. There was also a bird caller whose sound was exactly like a bird and was full of emotion. The performance was better than that of the Harmsdun group.

Taming of the Four Elephants Then, four elephants were brought out to walk around the ring. Then, each of them was made to sit on a chair, raise their front feet high, stand upright, and cry. Then, they climbed on each other to make various different performances. The elephants were extremely tame, so no giant ropes were added when they performed. When the two tigers came out, they were each tied with iron chains to prevent them from changing. In addition to the elephants and tigers, there was also a zebra, which I had never seen before in my life. The capital is great. After browsing around, I felt that the capital was really not comparable to ordinary entertainers. Even in terms of tents, it is already a great deal. In addition, the feeding of livestock and the salaries of the members of the group are not small. What is especially valuable is that the group also has a motor and a generator, each used to supply electricity. The power is imaginable.

Concerning Two Matters of "High-Interest Loans" 196

Recently, I heard about two matters concerning "high-interest loans." The first is quite amusing. Years ago, a certain Westerner residing in Nanyang opened a shoe store there. Due to a shortage of funds and difficulties in managing finances, compounded by being unfamiliar with the local people and unable to obtain loans, he reluctantly borrowed "high-interest loans" from Indians to alleviate his financial distress. At that time, the interest on "high-interest loans" was extremely high, with a rate of one-tenth of the principal per month. Even if the loan was not a full month, it was still counted as a month. If the loan was not repaid on time, the Indians would not hesitate to visit his store daily to demand repayment, some even bringing bedding and staying there until they got their money.

However, this Westerner borrowed money from dozens of Indian lenders, often failing to repay on time, yet he did not encounter any trouble with collections. Instead, the Indians trusted him and continued to lend him money. The reason was that the façade of his shoe store was impressively grand, with boxes of shoes piled up like mountains, giving the impression of substantial wealth. When the Indians came to collect their debts, the Westerner would point to the mountain of shoe boxes and say, "The goods have not been sold yet; I will pay you as soon as they are sold."

The Indians, seeing him as trustworthy, did not press for repayment. The Westerner, realizing the potential to deceive, borrowed more and more from the Indians, who did not refuse him despite the outstanding debts. Using this tactic, he fooled the Indians for a year. However, he knew that prolonged borrowing without repayment was not a sustainable strategy. Repaying the loans, including principal and interest, would amount to a staggering sum. Ultimately, he decided to abscond, stopping new shipments of goods. He sold off the remaining shoes in the store for cash, accumulated the funds, and left only empty shoe boxes stacked at the entrance, still giving the impression of a thriving business when the Indians came to inspect. The shoe store was on the verge of collapse.

The Westerner announced that he needed to return to his home country for a trip, entrusting the affairs of the store to a partner, and then left with his accumulated savings of over thirty thousand gold coins. Upon arriving home, he sent a letter to the partner, stating that he would not return and had no interest in the store's affairs. The partner reported the matter to the authorities and declared bankruptcy. Only then did the Indians awaken from their great dream, but it was all in vain. This story is widely known among those residing in Nanyang. The Westerner is truly contemptible, while the Indians are both pitiable and laughable.

In Shanghai, there was a carpenter whose income could not cover his expenses, and he often borrowed "high-interest loans" from an Indian to make ends meet. Later, the carpenter fell ill and was bedridden for five months. Without any income, his family's living expenses and medical bills were covered by further loans from the Indian, amounting to over two hundred gold coins. The carpenter was known to be poor and without any assets. The Indian continued to lend him money, not because he was sympathetic to his plight, but because he was interested in his daughter.

The carpenter's daughter, despite being from a humble background, was a beautiful young woman in her late teens. The Indian had long desired her and was willing to do anything to have her. One day, he directly approached the carpenter and said, "You owe me a considerable amount of money. Seeing your situation, I doubt you can repay me. How about you give me your daughter in marriage?" The carpenter was shocked to hear this. He owed a huge debt that he could not repay, and exchanging his daughter for money seemed like a viable option. He reluctantly agreed. He returned home and told his wife and daughter, and they all wept but were willing to comply.

A few days later, the Indian used gold to "buy" the beautiful woman and take her away. Soon after, the beautiful woman became haggard and lost her radiance. Within half a year, she passed away, like a fragrant flower fading. Alas, how tragic!

Discussing Chen Furu of Fuzhou, an Expert in Gold and Stone Inscriptions 197

Mr. Chen Furu, a renowned expert in gold and stone inscriptions, will open his second exhibition of works at the Ningbo Tongxiang Association on the 25th of this month. On display will be more than one hundred items, including fan ribs and seals, and rubbings will be distributed to guests. I, being fond of carving, was delighted to hear this and eagerly went to view the exhibit. Here are my observations for fellow enthusiasts:

Mr. Chen's given name is Furu, and his courtesy name is Qigang. He comes from a scholarly family in Pinghu. In his early years, he followed Mr. Huang Ainong of Changle in serving as an official in Fujian province. He has a deep love for gold and stone inscriptions, diligently and painstakingly dedicating himself to this art. The attainment of any skill requires time and effort. As the saying goes, "Achieving enlightenment depends on the individual."

Mr. Chen's seal carving possesses natural charm, regardless of the Zhejiang or Anhui styles. Mr. Jiang Cun called him "a man of all talents," and this is no exaggeration. His bamboo carving is also excellent in both calligraphy and painting, with superb knife techniques, avoiding ambiguity and combining strength and simplicity. I once saw a statue of an ancient Buddha he carved, with the inscription by Layman Zhong Xuan: "Paying homage to the Buddha of the Western Paradise, the ice pool is thoroughly clear." It was exquisite.

Mr. Chen then asked me, as a native of Jiaxing, about Jiaxing bamboo carving. Jiaxing bamboo carving has declined drastically in recent years, and most of the practitioners are unskilled amateurs with no real talent. I recalled that when I was a child, after copying Li Si's Yishan Stele, I saw carvers in the market carving the characters upwards, not following the brushstrokes of the seal script. I said, "Jiaxing bamboo carving will be ruined by these people." This is evident in this example. Recently, only the works of Shi Wenxiu and Zhang Wenyu are still worth seeing. Mr. Chen nodded in agreement.

Heartfelt Warmth (202) 198

Episode Eleven: The Beautiful Woman Returns to the Man of Worth, The Famous Courtesan Marries into a Prominent Family

Liu Xing Shu: Does Zhenhui know this? I'm telling you, this is a rare thing to encounter. Can the details of the situation be known?

Zuo Shi Chen: At least a friend told me that one day someone was hosting a dinner at a Western restaurant and everyone wanted to call for a "tang chang" [a public sing-song girl]. So I called for Ruiyun. After Ruiyun left, that friend told me, "Don't you know? Ruiyun is getting married!" I said, "Really?" He said, "I don't know if it will succeed, but they are in negotiations." By "negotiations," frankly speaking, they are discussing the price.

I asked, "Who is it?" He said, "It's someone named Zhao. I know him a little. He's very young, not even thirty yet, and very wealthy. He even has a garden." That person is not a vulgar man; he's dashing and romantic. I said, "That's good, I congratulate Ruiyun."

Liu Xing Shu: So, did you ask Ruiyun later, or did Ruiyun tell you?

Zuo Shi Chen: Don't be impatient, let me finish. Two days later, another friend invited me to a fancy dinner. This friend is also known to you, Yi Yunshang, who runs Zhu Feng's. That day was the last time the family was hosting guests. Aside from this, they don't invite friends to private dinners. You know your Zhu Feng's. Zhu Feng's room is right across from Ruiyun's house. When they got to Zhu Feng's, they called out, "(Add tea)" and the little girl from Ruiyun's side added a cup of tea.

I asked her, "Where's your Miss?" She said, "She's out singing "tang chang." I said, "Where's the madam?" She said, "She didn't come out today because she's sick in the small room." So, I didn't go over there. After Zhu Feng and the young ladies went out, he said to me, "Second Young Master, do you really like Ruiyun?" I said, "It's not that I like her or not. After getting familiar, I don't have to call for a "tang chang" that I don't know. When calling "tang chang", there is no need for so much talk to coax or not coax her, and don't need to get cold. If need to be get cold, why should call her?"

Zhu Feng said with a smile, "Everyone says you, Second Young Master, really like her, so there's no need to deny it." But Zhu Feng didn't finish. I said, "It's just what? The next thing is she's getting married, right?" Zhu Feng said, "Do you already know?" I said, "I even know who she's marrying, isn't it someone named Zhao, Zhao Qishao?" Zhu Feng said, "You're wrong, it's not someone named Zhao, but someone named Wu. I didn't know recently, because a friend named Wu also works with us, so they often come to my room to discuss this matter, and I've heard it all."

I said, "My news is also very accurate. So where did the person she's marrying come from?" Originally, I didn't want to ask Ruiyun, because I really wanted to ask her the truth about the Zhao-Wu issue.

The Bleak Future of the Textile Industry 209

Declining Exports, Plummeting Market Prices

Capital Reduction and Reduced Labor Seem Essential Strategies

Workers Prepare to Strike in Protest

Osaka, 27th - A dispatch from Japan reports that Japanese textile mills are currently employing short-time work systems in an effort to reduce cotton yarn production and maintain market prices. It is widely expected that in addition to the existing 17% reduction rate, cotton yarn production will be further reduced by 10% starting July 1st. Current cotton yarn production is 227,000 bales per month, and current yarn prices have reached their lowest point since 1916. This is due to numerous factors unfavorable to the industry, including a sudden decrease in textile exports. While cotton yarn inventories are not excessively large, cotton cloth inventories are rapidly increasing. Active wage cuts or large-scale layoffs of factory workers are likely unavoidable in the near future. Therefore, labor union leaders are preparing to fight this situation through strike action.

According to reports, Japanese Third Grade yarn prices have fallen rapidly in recent months, reaching a low of 139 yuan, the lowest since 1916. Since the government's decision to abolish night work on July 1, 1929, factories increased the number of spindles to avoid a reduction in production. As a result, cotton yarn production increased to over 260,000 bales per month, setting a new record. The establishment of the Hamaguchi Cabinet and the implementation of tight monetary policies following the lifting of the gold embargo dealt a significant blow to the financial sector. This hindered domestic sales of cotton yarn and negatively impacted overseas exports. Industry operators advocated for reduced working hours to decrease production. However, China, the primary market for Japanese yarn and cloth, experienced reduced sales due to competition from local Japanese factories. In India, a unanimous decision was made in April to increase cotton goods tariffs from 11% to 15%, with an additional 5% levy on British goods within three years. The Japanese cotton industry was shocked and, despite various attempts, failed to reverse the situation, leading to further difficulties in both domestic and foreign trade. Factories were forced to resort to capital reduction and workforce reduction measures. The large-scale strike at Kanebo, a leading company, was triggered by wage reductions. This illustrates the distress of the Japanese textile industry. The aforementioned telegram suggests a rather bleak outlook for the Japanese textile industry.

Art World

Saint Augustine, a New Italian Biography by Papini 219

Unexpectedly, Giovanni Papini, the author of "Story of Christ" (Storia di Cristo), has suddenly published a new book, "Saint Augustine" (Sant' Agostino). We all know that Saint Augustine is a great figure in Catholicism, and his deeds have inspired countless writers and scholars in various countries around the world. There have been many books written about him. Étienne Gilson of France published "Introduction à l'étude de Saint Augustin" not long ago.

Now Papini has also come out with a "Saint Augustine". Is he trying to capitalize on the current trend of romantic biographies, the so-called "new biographical literature"? However, no, Papini has not been tempted by this. Of course, it would be easy for him to follow the fashionable approach, because Saint Augustine is not only a great "saint" but also a great "mortal". The romantic elements in his life provide ample material for a romantic biography. But Papini refuses to do so. We must remember that Papini is a naturally argumentative person. He is always opposed to the prevailing opinions of his time. In his own eyes, Papini is almost a creator, revolutionary, destructive, inspiring, creative, a hero, a reformer, a saint, and someone who once tried to write "Story of Christ" in the first-person singular as if he were "walking the path of God". Therefore, after he finished writing "Story of Christ", it was inevitable that he would write "Story of Augustine", because he has always held a personal, autobiographical view of literature and history. Moreover, the saint who wrote "Confessions" and the writer who wrote "Story of Christ" share spiritual similarities. Saint Augustine was a rhetorician, a Latinist, a grammarian, a Neo-Platonist philosopher, and a writer of paradoxical arguments. He was ultimately dissatisfied with everything. He was a mirror in which Papini was reflected, but on a grander scale. Papini himself tells the reader frankly:

It seems to me that there is a certain resemblance between us. He is also a man of letters and a lover of words, and a creator of philosophy and truth who is harassed, even tempted by "Occultism". He is also carnal, seeking fame. I am like him, naturally like his worst parts, but in any case, I am always like him.

Saint Augustine was first a sinner and later became a saint. Papini has always had deep sympathy for him. But this sympathy alone is not a sufficient reason for Papini to write "Saint Augustine". It is not only because of the similarity in Western temperament, but also because there is a very important and deep connection between them. This connection is that they are both Catholic writers and both underwent major spiritual upheavals before converting to Catholicism. After experiencing countless intellectual truths, they finally found spiritual peace. In our opinion, this book is Papini's answer. The question is, "Papini, why did you convert to Catholicism?" Papini seems to answer, "Look at this man, he is much greater than I. Look at how he chose his path. I have done nothing but follow in his footsteps."

················

In the preface of this book, Papini solemnly declares his purpose in writing it:

My purpose is to retell the external and internal life of this great African man with the greatest simplicity, clearly indicating where the certain facts end and the probable conjectures begin. Of course, this is not to explain "Confessions" again line by line, because that book only goes up to the age of thirty-three and does not continue. However, the intention of this book is not to fully explain the thoughts of this great saint, because to say nothing of the entirety of his thoughts, even a general discussion of his philosophy, his theology, or his mysticism would make this book even longer. So my intention is only to tell the story of a soul.

But after reading this book, we cannot help but say that Papini's explanation is somewhat unconvincing, because the general reader would rather Papini frankly choose one of two paths: either purely create a work of art, as his reputation demands, or write a history on the subject. But now Papini is not taking either of these paths. His current work can slightly arouse our attention, but it does not make us read it attentively or enthusiastically. As for the soul of Augustine, although he says he wants to write a history of this soul, he rarely depicts this soul. When he does depict it, it is indeed depicted very powerfully, but unfortunately he loves to write about passions too much, especially those base passions. Of course, we can also see from this that Papini, like Augustine, indulges in carnal passions and likes to talk about them often. However, this is somewhat contradictory to his own statement.

After all, "fame is difficult to live up to". His position is too high, and readers' expectations for him are inevitably too high. What he gives us in this book is indeed very different from what we hope to get from this book. What he gives us is neither romance nor history, but a genuine picture of a saint's life and the times in which he lived, written in a calm and light style. Of course, there are a few pages in this book that are written very beautifully, such as the last chapter.

The Story of World Literature (163, by John Macy, translated by Hu Zhongchi) 220

Chapter 41: German Literature After Goethe

We have arrived at the doorstep of modern times. Here we encounter the singular figure of the poet and philosopher Friedrich Nietzsche. Nietzsche is, first and foremost, an artist, a great artist. He is also a thinker who has spoken to humanity more than anyone else about the most central teachings of modern thought, believing that morality, like the material world, is something that changes and lives, not something that is unchanging and dead. Therefore, man can completely transcend his present self. This idea of change and the superman is a seed, a yeast that ferments the entirety of modern life. What makes this and everything that follows shine like a flame is the incomparable power of Nietzsche's words. Not only in "Thus Spoke Zarathustra", but also in all of his other works, in "The Revaluation of All Values", in "Human, All Too Human", we encounter the great creative speaker. His words burn, fly, and sing. His books carry a message that resonates in the hearts of the people of this new era, with a persuasiveness and eloquence comparable to that of the Gospels, and the ecstatic beauty of his language. His books are full of deeply meaningful aphorisms, which unfold new vistas towards "man and nature and life". And above all, he also possesses the mark of a wise man who is also a poet, who gives life and breath to those aphorisms, often making them part of the structure of a lyrical poem, a fable. To understand the latest revolution in German literature, we must remember that in 1880, Hebbel, Keller, Meyer, and Nietzsche were not yet fully famous. The public was watching inferior dramas imitating the works of Augier and Dumas fils, and reading sentimental novels and poems drained from the dregs of Romanticism, lacking original beauty and power. Then the young people of the early 1880s rose up in rebellion, organized societies, published manifestos, promoted the theory of thorough naturalism, and established a powerful literary movement. Arno Holz's pamphlets and models soon bore fruit. The true poets Detlev von Liliencron and the great playwright Gerhart Hauptmann appeared. The novel was slightly behind, but this was not for long. A new literature was born.

Together with Liliencron, the lyrical poetry, often the glory of German literature, regained its precise and sharp and true character. His songs and folk songs, in the midst of them, contained soldiers and wine and bread. And at the same time, although he precisely and vividly arranged small things, he discovered for German poetry the beautiful, rigorous forms. Under the leadership of Liliencron, lyrical poetry burst forth. The next and perhaps the most outstanding poet of all is Richard Dehmel. To Liliencron's brilliance and precision, Dehmel added a philosophical imagination and power that transferred the entire spirit of modern life, the mechanical complexity, into poetry. In this respect, he stands apart from the poets of Europe. He could write folk songs and also write with the simplicity of medieval hymns. However, in a hundred individual poems and in the legend of "Two Souls", his most remarkable achievement lies in creating modern men and women living on bicycles, making telephone calls, writing poems about women playing the piano next door, and speaking of these things with poems that are vivid and noble.

Art World Guidelines 221

(1) Articles should be limited to news, reviews, and introductions about recent art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature, both domestic and foreign.

(2) Traditional Chinese painting should be limited to new works by domestic and foreign artists and accompanying images related to the text.

(3) Photographs should be limited to recent portraits and works by domestic and foreign artists and various photographs related to the text.

(4) The maximum length of each article should not exceed 3,000 characters.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, and do not write illegibly. Western languages should be abbreviated where possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink for illustrations in the manuscript, and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and black ink.

(8) Please indicate that submissions should be addressed to the Art World Department.

(9) Submissions will not be returned regardless of whether they are published. If a return is required, it should be stated in advance and sufficient postage should be attached.

(10) Remuneration for articles is divided into three types: four yuan, three yuan, and two yuan per thousand characters. The same applies to illustrations and photographs. Special manuscripts will be remunerated separately.

Publishing News 222

The Zhongyi Book Bureau in Maijiaquan, Shandong Road, Shanghai, announces that Mr. Qin Bowen of Shanghai is the nephew of Mr. Qin Xitian, the director of the Shanghai Local Property Office. He studied medicine at a young age and has considerable expertise. He has served as the director of education and professor of Internal Medicine at the Shanghai Chinese Medicine College, the China Medical College, and the National Pharmaceutical Association. In addition to medicine, he is also skilled in epigraphy, calligraphy, painting, and poetry. To celebrate his thirtieth birthday, his friends have compiled and printed his poems from the past ten years or so into a large volume titled "Poems of Tai Bowen", finely printed in the Juzhen edition. In addition to distributing copies to friends and relatives, there are over two hundred copies available. To make friends with fellow poets, each copy is priced at only two dimes (two jiao) to cover printing costs. Anyone interested in studying poetry can contact the book bureau to obtain a copy.

Ouyang Xin and Sun Ren Shan were elected as the editors of the editorial section, Zhang Yi Sheng and Ye Jiong Xing as the heads of the publicity section, and Ji Wei Xin and Zhang Zhi Guo as the heads of the solicitation section. Famous masterpieces will also be published in this magazine.

Tongchang Automobile Company of Nanjing Road announces that because bicycles cannot be mailed, this company has imported bicycles from the famous German Huituola factory that can be disassembled. After testing, the structure of this bicycle frame is extremely precise. When packed and shipped, the rear frame can be disassembled, taking up only half the space. The post office can also mail it to other locations, making procurement very convenient. Moreover, the bicycle is sturdy and lightweight, with a unique paint color and genuine chrome steel rims that will never rust. These are now on display and all are welcome to visit. Due to the limited number of sample bicycles available, each person is limited to purchasing only one.

Dahua Food Company, located at the intersection of Xian Gua Street and Dongmen Road outside Xiaodongmen, announces that this company specializes in famous Jiang Tui ham, floral dew fruit wine, sanitary pickles, etc. Since the establishment of the direct sales department, business has been booming. In view of the upcoming Dragon Boat Festival, this company is offering a ten-day grand sale on gifts needed by all sectors of society. Therefore, the store has been crowded in recent days, with more customers than can be served.

China Samsung Company announces that the quality of our country's ink has always been poor, and the written words are easily smeared and altered. In recent years, cases of tampering with checks, account books, wills, and other important documents have become increasingly common. People in all sectors of society are paying attention to this matter. As a result, scientists have begun to research a new method to prevent fraud, which is to replace ordinary ink with a product called Insurance Ink. The inventor is chemist Huang Letian. After drying, the color of this Insurance Ink is not only exceptionally glossy, but the written words have been tested by soaking in clear water for three months without any blurring. Attempts to wash it with chemical solutions also failed to remove the words. This shows that the ink adheres to the paper in such a way that it cannot be altered, thus preventing fraud. Although Insurance Ink is a common commodity, it has important functions. Therefore, all checks, drafts, account books, wills, official documents, notices, and important documents in all sectors should be written with Insurance Ink. Insurance Ink is produced by this company and is now available on the market.

Dahua Woolen Mill announces that Mr. Gu Jiuru, a giant in the industrial sector, has been deeply concerned about the decline of the domestic woolen industry and the fact that imports of foreign goods exceed hundreds of millions of yuan each year, causing a great loss of economic benefits. He has spared no expense in spending several years of effort to research and manufacture domestic gabardine woolen cloth, with excellent results. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce of the National Government has issued a top-grade commendation certificate to encourage him. Mr. Gu has established this woolen mill at the end of Gordon Road and West Suzhou Road, specializing in the production of domestic striped and plain gabardine and various woolen cloths. The products are exquisitely made and the colors are fashionable. To promote domestic goods, the prices are especially low. The wholesale location of this factory is at Zhaofuli, across from the Xinwen Bao newspaper office on Sanma Road. Samples will be sent immediately upon request from woolen cloth dealers in this city or other cities.

Zhao Junmou Pharmacy, No. 355, Qiujiang East Road, North Sichuan Road, announces that this pharmacy has recently invented a bedbug pesticide that can be sprayed with a device to kill bedbugs, fleas, mosquitoes, and flies. It also has disinfectant properties. Since its launch, it has been very popular and highly effective.

Theater News 225

Nanjing Grand Theater announces that starting today, it will screen the complete sound and dialogue tragic film "Torrent of Sin," starring Marena Lauren. The film tells the story of a young woman whose will is intoxicated by the colors and revelry of the city, causing her to abandon her family and mix into the tide. The plot twists and turns, providing viewers with ample emotional stimulation. At the same time, the complete sound and dialogue comedy film "Cohabitation Love," starring the hilarious star Deng Nanshi, will also be screened. It tells the story of a wealthy young man who forces a beautiful woman to cohabit with him, creating a lot of laughs. In addition, three famous new plays performed by Mei Lanfang, the king of the Chinese opera world, during his tour of the United States on Broadway will also be shown at the same time, creating an unprecedented spectacle in Shanghai.

Mingxing Film Company announces that Peach Blossom Lake is the latest blockbuster film directed by Zheng Zhengqiu of this company. The actors are all famous male and female stars of the time, such as Hu Die, Zheng Xiaoqiu, Xia Peizhen, Wang Xianzai, and Huang Junfu, who all play extremely important roles in the film. The three leading actors, Hu, Zheng, and Xia, have received in-depth acting training from director Zheng. The release of this film will be their most successful work. Director Zheng has put more effort into the study of action, performance, portrayal, and the individuality of each person, striving for further artistic advancement in every aspect.

Portuguese Dance Troupe announces that this troupe is a non-professional organization established by the Cantonese overseas Chinese student community in Shanghai. It has served the community many times in its three years of existence and has been highly praised by the general public. Recently, the troupe plans to hold its first public performance, with programs including "Three Butterflies" and other newly created song and dance dramas. The troupe members, such as Ms. Cheng Yuzhen, Ms. He Huifang, Ms. Zhu Biyun, and Ms. Huang Wenxiu, are all excellent singers and dancers. Ms. Wu Peixian, who was once famous for her singing and dancing but has not appeared in public for a long time, will also perform. Samsung Stage announces that this stage has recently been arranging the patriotic opera "Serving the Country with Utmost Loyalty." This play is based on Li Guichun's secret script, which has been greatly revised and expanded. It is now being rehearsed and the opening date is not far off. At that time, there will definitely be a large crowd.

Xifan Film Company announces that this company has recently produced two new films, named "Love in the Heavens" and "Four Heroes" and "Passionate Swordsman," starring Wang Feijuan, Cheng Jingxiong, Ai Yajuan, Xu Zhongxia, Pu Xianying, Lu Zhongxia and others.
